  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d0b22eae-aee0-4ff7-91fc-116e0504f3ad'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1436278406556818109">Geheimnisvolle Türen mit Eidechsenknäufen, sprechende Steinfiguren und ein wildgewordenes Kindermädchen mit einem Beil ...   <span id="freeText1436278406556818109" style="display:none">Geheimnisvolle Türen mit Eidechsenknäufen, sprechende Steinfiguren und ein wildgewordenes Kindermädchen mit einem Beil ... Liv Silbers Träume sind in der letzten Zeit ziemlich unheimlich. Besonders einer von ihnen beschäftigt sie sehr. In diesem Traum war sie auf einem Friedhof, bei Nacht, und hat vier Jungs bei einem düsteren magischen Ritual beobachtet. Zumindest die Jungs stellen aber eine ganz reale Verbindung zu Livs Leben dar, denn Grayson und seine drei besten Freunde gibt es wirklich. Seit kurzem geht Liv auf dieselbe Schule wie die vier. Eigentlich sind sie ganz nett. Wirklich unheimlich - noch viel unheimlicher als jeder Friedhof bei Nacht - ist jedoch, dass die Jungs Dinge über sie wissen, die sie tagsüber nie preisgegeben hat - wohl aber im Traum. Kann das wirklich sein? Wie sie das hinbekommen ist ihr absolut rätselhaft, aber einem guten Rätsel konnte Liv noch nie widerstehen...</span>
  <a data-text-id="1436278406556818109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/551719-reading-the-english-version-i-am">Reading the English version...

I am curious as to how this book has been translated. How much has been changed in the translation from the German? 
For example, in the original;
Is Lottie English? Or is she still German
Is the poem that is her dream door&#39;s protection still a German poem?
Is it still set in London?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_551719'><a id="like_count_community_question_551719" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/551719?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F17566243-silber">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/551719-reading-the-english-version-i-am">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/551719-reading-the-english-version-i-am">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/68774971-katie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1594816274i/68774971._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/68774971-katie">Katie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Well, when translating books they don't generally change things like this. The characters always live in the same places and have the same origin. Jus<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Well, when translating books they don't generally change things like this. The characters always live in the same places and have the same origin. Just like the German version of Harry Potter is still set in Britain and Harry and the Dursleys still live in Surrey. Lottie is obviously still German (Bavarian, to be precise) and therefore, the poem is in German, too. And Liv and her family obviously still live in England, though her father is originally German, which is why their last name is Silber and not Silver. You see, when translating a book the translators are really only... well, translating. They're not supposed to change the story or even write a completely new one. Depending on the book they might change people's or places' names (e.g. A Song of Ice and Fire does that a lot and it even happens in Harry Potter every once in a while) but they would never change the setting or anything like that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1701145224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701145224" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701145224?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701145224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18176955730393078584">Hngh. This book's difficult. I'm not even sure I rated it correctly. I've been in a massive reading slump lately, and I've been seriously flagging with my reading challenge, which is disappointing, since I was smashing it for the first half of the year. Until about May, I was never less than 3 books ahead. Now I'm three books behind and bricking it. I thought this book might pull me from my funk, but it was a bust. <br/><br/>This book was a pretty quick, easy read, and the best thing about it is the narra</span>
  <span id="freeText18176955730393078584" style="display:none">Hngh. This book's difficult. I'm not even sure I rated it correctly. I've been in a massive reading slump lately, and I've been seriously flagging with my reading challenge, which is disappointing, since I was smashing it for the first half of the year. Until about May, I was never less than 3 books ahead. Now I'm three books behind and bricking it. I thought this book might pull me from my funk, but it was a bust. <br /><br />This book was a pretty quick, easy read, and the best thing about it is the narrative voice; I loved Liv's character, loved her narration, loved her careful balance between dry and joyful. I usually hate this "woe is me, I have too much money and too many opportunities" narrative trend in a lot of YA, but Gier strikes a nice balance between Liv's hermitic loneliness and her easygoing nature. I related to it, which is saying quite a lot. It's also been brilliantly translated from its original German, which helps. <br /><br />The problem is that this book just didn't make sense; it was like an acid trip, and not in a good way. Not in a pleasantly disorienting way. In a way that made me wonder if my copy was missing pages. It's not really about Liv instantly becoming friends with these Londoner Raven Boys, which is unlikely but not impossible - I did a two-day intensive TEFL course in Glasgow a few weeks ago, and after about an hour in a class of 15 students, we were all soul mates. I mean it. We'd have taken a bullet for each other. When I was querying my manuscript, I had an agent tell me that it was weird that the protagonist makes such fast friends when she moves to a new city, but I swear to god, meet the right people in the right setting and you really can experience the gush of instalove. Sometimes I think about the people I met in that classroom, people I knew for a maximum of 20 hours and will never see again, and I pine. <br /><br />But it's more about the way that none of the characters get freaked out by this whole dreamscape thing, and nobody thinks it's weird, and then there's the strange ball, and I know I'm not explaining this very well, but it was all so surreal. Like <i>The Mighty Boosh</i>. (<i>What</i> the fuck was that all about.) I'm not getting my point across very well, probably because it was something I couldn't put my finger on - maybe the atmosphere, or something like that. It was just bizarre. <br /><br />I haven't read Gier's Ruby Red series, and I'm not sure I'll bother, because I just really don't care for stories about London. I'm done with them for now. I don't want to read anything else about London. But this book was a strange mishmash for me, and while I'd love to read more of Liv's voice, I don't think I can really justify throwing myself back into this psychedelic funhouse for another 300 pages. I have better things to do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18176955730393078584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I am definitely interested in reading the author's Ruby Red trilogy now, though. I like the way she writes, I just hope the plot and characters are a bit more clear cut in her other series. Seems like other people are liking this one better, which I understand--I just haven't the patience for this right now.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10464259635119889344">Upon 2017 reread: original review stands. Fun and entertaining. Finally continuing on with this series. <br/><br/>————————————————————<br/><br/>This book was unexpectedly good! I am not going to lie, from the blurb, I was picturing a sort of The Raven Boys knock off story and the only similarities is that there are dreams, and 4 boys and a girl. Otherwise, they are nothing alike!<br/><br/>Dream a Little Dream follows a hilarious girl named Olivia who moves to London and meets 4 boys in a dream one night, and these same four </span>
  <span id="freeText10464259635119889344" style="display:none">Upon 2017 reread: original review stands. Fun and entertaining. Finally continuing on with this series. <br /><br />————————————————————<br /><br />This book was unexpectedly good! I am not going to lie, from the blurb, I was picturing a sort of The Raven Boys knock off story and the only similarities is that there are dreams, and 4 boys and a girl. Otherwise, they are nothing alike!<br /><br />Dream a Little Dream follows a hilarious girl named Olivia who moves to London and meets 4 boys in a dream one night, and these same four boys go to her school. What ensues next is Liv, using her love for solving problems, trying to figure out what the boys are up to, and how she fits in to everything. <br /><br />The best part of the book is by far the characters. Really diverse and intricate characters. All have a unique voice and really bring something to the story. <br /><br />Plot wise this book was great! I love the creativity of the story. I love the pacing. Never too fast or too slow. I felt like every scene was necessary and helped further the plot in some way. I also love the ending because it has a bit of an open ending, but if this was a stand alone I wouldn't mind.<br /><br />I truly adored this book and I hope that book 2 and 3 get translated to English soon!<br /><br />I definitely recommend this book, and probably the entire trilogy, to everyone who like a bit of a light fantasy read with nothing overly complicated.</span>

<div id="review_1256513609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256513609" />
    <a title="Aditi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16069171-aditi"><img alt="Aditi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480260251p2/16069171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1256513609?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aditi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aditi" href="/user/show/16069171-aditi">Aditi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=friends">friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=macmillan">macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=pan-mc">pan-mc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256513609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7454041680401272355"> <i>“All that we see or seem is but a dream within a dream.” </i><br/><br/> ---- Edgar Allan Poe<br/><br/><br/>Kerstin Gier, a German bestselling author's Silver trilogy is being translated into English by the popular English translator, Anthea Bell. So the translated version of the first book in this series, <i>Dream a Little Dream</i> has been released this month, that centers around the life of an unconventional teenager who is admitted to a new English school in London and so as her dreams take a new turn, exciting adventures are</span>
  <span id="freeText7454041680401272355" style="display:none"> <i>“All that we see or seem is but a dream within a dream.” </i><br /><br /> ---- Edgar Allan Poe<br /><br /><br />Kerstin Gier, a German bestselling author's Silver trilogy is being translated into English by the popular English translator, Anthea Bell. So the translated version of the first book in this series, <i>Dream a Little Dream</i> has been released this month, that centers around the life of an unconventional teenager who is admitted to a new English school in London and so as her dreams take a new turn, exciting adventures are waiting for her that will change her life.<br /><br /><br /><b>Synopsis: </b><br /><br /><i>Mysterious doors with lizard-head knobs. Talking stone statues. A crazy girl with a hatchet. Yes, Liv’s dreams have been pretty weird lately. Especially this one where she’s in a graveyard at night, watching four boys conduct dark magic rituals.<br /><br />The strangest part is that Liv recognizes the boys in her dream. They’re classmates from her new school in London, the school where she’s starting over because her mom has moved them to a new country (again). But what’s really scaring Liv is that the dream boys seem to know things about her in real life, things they couldn’t possibly know—unless they actually are in her dreams? Luckily, Liv could never resist a good mystery, and all four of those boys are pretty cute. </i><br /><br /><br />Liv Silver, a 15 year old teenager leads a pretty unconventional life compare to her age, mainly because of her mom's constantly changing jobs, she has got to live and see a lot of new places and this time her mom's new job and her mom's new boyfriend, leads her straight to London along with her Mia and the au pair named, Lottie. Liv is enrolled into one of the poshest school in London, Frognal Academy, where girls have stupid names and boys are terribly hot with great hair and everybody is subjected to their school's very own blog, Tittle-Tattle Blog, with an anonymous author. Following her entry to this new school, her dreams started to get weirder and weirder, where no doubt she could see her number one crush from her school, Henry and in someone she feels her dreams her actually real. And eventually Liv started investigating those dreams and what she finds out is not at all nice and friendly.<br /><br /><br />Having never read any of the previous books by this author, I had no idea what to expect from her writing style, but from the very first page, itself, I was drawn into the story, mainly because of Liv's sense of humor and her witty demeanor of cracking up jokes with her sarcastic comments. Yes, I can vouch for Liv and say that she is the life of this book, without her the journey would be very dull. <br /><br />The pacing of the book is good, but I believe that the translation is not much polished compared to the original book. Liv's fun-filled adventures certainly kept me going through the book, well since it falls under middle-grade genre, the mystery felt bit predictable layered with childish drama.<br /><br />The characters apart from Liv are not that impressionable, especially those four boys, except that hot, sultry looks! Yes, there is romance between Henry and Liv which is sweet and innocent, but the author never shifts her focus from the main theme of the book which is the mystery surrounding Liv's dream.<br /><br />So if you want to delve deeper into the worlds of dreams and wants to float in them, then do read this cute and funny book that is filled with thrilling adventures.<br /><br /><b>Verdict: </b> <i>Drams worlds with strange door knobs, fantasy world, Gossip Girl kinda feel with some hot dudes- if these are things that you love to read about, then definitely go for this book. </i><br /><br /><b>Courtesy: </b> <i>Thanks to the author's publicist, for giving me an opportunity to read and review this book. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7454041680401272355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1255798686" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255798686" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563502369p2/23218431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1255798686?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=eyeroll-moments">eyeroll-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=slooooowww">slooooowww</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=annoying-tropes">annoying-tropes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1255798686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16553546434318297385">I have been stalling to read this series for 2 years, but I think I am ready now. One of my absolute favorite trilogies was written by Kerstin Gier and I am really hoping this one would be just as amazing, if not more.<br/><br/>Also, that cover is GORGEOUS.<br/>-------------------------------<br/><u>Thoughts on the 1st half of the book</u><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“But maybe I wasn’t doing the film justice and it wasn’t the usual high school garbage with the malicious blond cheerleader, the charming but superficial football captain, and the imp</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16553546434318297385" style="display:none">I have been stalling to read this series for 2 years, but I think I am ready now. One of my absolute favorite trilogies was written by Kerstin Gier and I am really hoping this one would be just as amazing, if not more.<br /><br />Also, that cover is GORGEOUS.<br />-------------------------------<br /><u>Thoughts on the 1st half of the book</u><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“But maybe I wasn’t doing the film justice and it wasn’t the usual high school garbage with the malicious blond cheerleader, the charming but superficial football captain, and the impoverished, beautiful outsider with a heart of gold.”</i>
</blockquote><br />---Damn… Kerstin Gier calling them out, and I. Am. Here. For. It.<br />I forgot how relatable her characters were.<br /><br />I’m not really the type to laugh when a funny scene appears in a book/movie. Not because I don’t find it funny, but because I’m more of an “internal laughter” type of person (wow, way to sound creepy) However, this book had me outright choking out laughter – and I just love it. <b>Liv, the protagonist, said the most hilariously relatable things.</b><br /><br />The plot was interesting. Slow, but definitely different. Liv, started sharing dreams with other people – dreams where she and the others could do pretty much anything (like fly), enter other people’s dreams, and communicate with one another. <b>It was very eerie at times and incredibly fun at others seeing Liv discover how these dreams worked.</b> I mean, would I like to be able to do anything in my dreams, go anywhere, see anyone??? Fuck yeah, that’d be awesome! Unfortunately for me, I’m never aware that I’m dreaming in my dreams so no control here. <br /><br /><u>Thoughts on the 2nd half of the book</u><br /><b>Honestly, I got bored.</b> The plot was not really moving anywhere. So much secrecy, so little answers. It did not feel progressive. The bits of mysteries and reveals speckled throughout the book did not make me more curious. I just felt disinterested and was waiting for something amazing to happen. It didn’t really.<br /><br />Also, I felt like the characters got a bit dull. Don’t get me wrong. <b>I really liked some of them, such as Liv’s sweet nanny named Lottie and her adorable, funny sister named Mia.</b> The thing that was lacking was in the friendship department. <b>Because a good part of the book was set at school, it sucked to see that most of the girls we met were so…nasty.</b> They were boys-obsessed or superficial or just plain ugh. I know this is a “YA book,” and these books often times have that, but can we get anymore cliché? Thus, Liv had one “female friend” at this school named Persephone – who was also one of those superficial, boy-obsessed girls – and what was more unpleasant that Liv hung out with her everyday even though she found Persephone annoying AF and didn’t even like her. And it’s like, <i>What are you doing, Liv????</i> I suppose Liv’s sole support system would be Mia, her sister, but despite the apparent closeness that we saw at the beginning between them, I was somewhat surprise that Liv did not even THINK or debate on telling Mia about her weird dreams. Not that she should, but she did not even consider it, which was weird when she treated Mia almost like a best friend at the beginning of the book.<br /><br />Furthermore, a big focus of the book was on these 4 “hot, popular” guys at school (no, not the Raven boys). A bit of a cliché, but I’m OK with that. <b>My problem was that we did not really see any developments or true connection among them.</b> Clearly, they were “best friends,” but I did not feel the chemistry. I just felt blah about them, which was disappointing. In addition, Liv’s dreams and her agreement to pretty much save all their asses – I felt like that should have made the boys want to actually KNOW her, or at least feel more appreciative. However, she just said yes, and they told her only part of the plans, and that’s it. No real development after that. I thought she was going to get included in the group somehow because she was an integral part of their mission afterall.<br /><br /><b>These characters were not developed very well in my opinion,</b> except for maybe Henry and Grayson. Henry – because he was the love interest of Liv, and Grayson – because he was sorta-kinda her brother now. Arthur and Jasper – I did not get a good grasp on their characters, but all four boys as a whole were just blah for being a central part of the book. With that being said, I’m hoping that these characters would become less bland and more endearing in the future books.<br /><br />I liked the romance in the book. It was a bit cheesy and sudden, but still very cute. <b>There was some cute bantering and funny and sweet moments.</b> My problem with Henry would be his secrecy but I’m not too concerned about that for now because there are still 2 more books to go. I can’t wait for more developments because this could easily become the best thing ever or just go up in flames. <br /><br /><u>Final Thoughts</u><br />I’m giving it <b>3 stars</b>. I certainly like certain components of the book, like the initial plot, the humor, the romance, and Liv’s family, but a lot of the core things, such as the slow development of the plot and characters, and the rather unpleasant school setting and friendships were disappointing. And because I have to – I am going to compare this with <i>The Ruby Red Trilogy</i>, also by Kerstin Gier. I have to say that Ruby Red is certainly better in pretty much every aspect – the plot is better-paced and more fun, the characters are more endearing and funny, and the protagonist is just…perfect. However, the one thing that this series perhaps has done better (judging by this 1st book) is the romance. At this moment, I like Henry more than Gideon. Anyway, I am curious about how the future books will develop. <b>It has been overall a fun first book with a lot of promise, even if I am disappointed with some aspects of it.</b><br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Is there a happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cliffhanger, not the last book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, no, low-medium angst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scene? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think, in general, the book starts out really well. Good vibes, fun meeting the main character and the others. I can’t quite a pinpoint a particularly scene though. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Teens and up. It’s rather innocent, but there are vague mentions of sex and virginity and getting drunk (which is what to be expected in a high school setting). Were there actual scenes of sex or mature scenes? No.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16553546434318297385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko"><img alt="Katerina  Kondrenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590049412p2/36306002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114250055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4082088193388401257"><blockquote>
  <b>10 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2015/03/silber-das-erste-buch-der-traume-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: fantasy, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: dream-walkers, a lot of fun<br/><b>WOW</b>: original concept, humor<br/><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: light <br/><br/><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>
    "It's in dreams more than anywhere else that you get to know people best - along with their weaknesses and their secrets."
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>I've read it in </span>
  <span id="freeText4082088193388401257" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>10 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br /><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br /><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2015/03/silber-das-erste-buch-der-traume-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br /><br /><b>Genre</b>: fantasy, YA<br /><b>Stuff</b>: dream-walkers, a lot of fun<br /><b>WOW</b>: original concept, humor<br /><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br /><b>Love-Geometry</b>: light <br /><br /><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>
    "It's in dreams more than anywhere else that you get to know people best - along with their weaknesses and their secrets."
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I've read it in Russian and have to admit that our translator did a good job! The last time I was laughing so hard was my Angelfall-reading. I don’t know what this book like in English and I don’t know German but hope you guys had (or would have) as much fun as did I. <br /><br />I really liked “Precious Stone Trilogy”: it was simple, funny and cute. I’d been shelving “Silber” for a few months, ‘cause I thought I'd be kinda disappointed or this book would turn out to be very similar to “Precious…”. I was worrying for nothing. <b>From the very first pages I got that I will love this series. Near to 30% I even made a sacrifice to the god of awesome books</b> (by eating some halva while reading the book, I think this god is a sweet-tooth, also I have no goats). <br /><br />What do we have here?<br /><br /><b>A Family #1</b>: an extravagant and a bit of babish mother who moves from one country to another because of her work contracts (she’s professor), 13 and 16 year old sisters with good wits, a nanny-for-all-occasions Lottie who sometimes twists English in a very funny way, and a cute and active dog.<br /> <br /><b>A Family #2</b>: a calm and wise dad, 17 year old twins (a daughters who wanna be the best in everything and a son who's more like his dad and can call a demon), a cute and passive cat. <br /><br /><u>
  <i>The Family #1 + The Family #2 --&gt; under the same roof = LOL</i>
</u> <br /><br /><b>But this is just a taste of what's to come!</b><br /><br />Lucid dreaming, British Gossip Girl and her blog, four handsome seniors who want something (and fast) from our MC named Liv, a demon who can fulfill your wishes and wants to break loose into our world, school days and teenage problems. And it’s all set out in a very laughable manner! <br /><br />But lord forbid you to look in this book for strong sense, morals etc. If you pick up “Silber”, you should remember for what/who and why this thing was published. <i>There will be naivety, mismatches, predictability, but you will love this because of its writing style.</i><br /><br />It’s like communication with people. You can be clever, wise and thoughtful but uninteresting and boring. On the other hand, you can be as plain as day, but friendly, nice, with a great sense of humor. I bet that people would love to pass the time with the second you. And "Silber" is just like that.<br /><br /><b>Silber Trilogie (Трилогия сновидений):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114250055" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das erste Buch der Träume (Зильбер. Первая книга сновидений)</a> #1/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114251314" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das zweite Buch der Träume (Зильбер. Вторая книга сновидений)</a> #2/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249925431" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das dritte Buch der Träume (Зильбер. Третья книга сновидений)</a> #3/3</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2710123611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2710123611" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2710123611?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9655338086224967270">I’m quite pleased to say that I enjoyed this book way more than I thought I would! I really didn’t enjoy another series by this author so I was a bit skeptical about this one and definitely proved me wrong. It was an incredibly interesting concept and definitely unlike anything I’ve ever read. I also loved that it was a hell of a lot darker than I thought it would be and I was all for it. Demons and dream walking? Sign me up! My only minor complaint is that the relationships between the characte</span>
  <span id="freeText9655338086224967270" style="display:none">I’m quite pleased to say that I enjoyed this book way more than I thought I would! I really didn’t enjoy another series by this author so I was a bit skeptical about this one and definitely proved me wrong. It was an incredibly interesting concept and definitely unlike anything I’ve ever read. I also loved that it was a hell of a lot darker than I thought it would be and I was all for it. Demons and dream walking? Sign me up! My only minor complaint is that the relationships between the characters kind of annoyed me at times and it affected my enjoyment of the book slightly.</span>

<div id="review_1225852294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225852294" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225852294?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225852294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11258183996215480007">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/03/review-dream-little-dream-by-kerstin.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Dream A Little Dream by Kerstin Gier<br/>Book One of the Silver Trilogy<br/>Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR) <br/>Publication Date: April 14, 2015<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Mysterious doors with lizard-head knobs. Talking stone statues. A crazy girl with a hatchet. Yep, Liv’s dreams have been pretty weird lately. Especially this one where she’s in a graveyard at night, watching four boys perform dark magic rituals. </span>
  <span id="freeText11258183996215480007" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/03/review-dream-little-dream-by-kerstin.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Dream A Little Dream by Kerstin Gier<br />Book One of the Silver Trilogy<br />Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR) <br />Publication Date: April 14, 2015<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Mysterious doors with lizard-head knobs. Talking stone statues. A crazy girl with a hatchet. Yep, Liv’s dreams have been pretty weird lately. Especially this one where she’s in a graveyard at night, watching four boys perform dark magic rituals. <br /><br />The really weird thing is that Liv recognizes the boys in her dream. They’re classmates from her new school in London, the school where’s she’s starting over because her mom has moved them to a new country (again). But they seem to know things about her in real life that they couldn't possibly know, which is mystifying. Then again, Liv could never resist a good mystery. . . .<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Kerstin Gier does it again! I wish all of her books could be picked up by USA publishers, because I've been quite in love with her books since Ruby Red was published in the United States, in 2011. The Ruby Red trilogy is one of my favorite series of all time!<br /><br />In this new series, Liv is leaving one place for another, but her new home has some... interesting people to it. Her and her younger sister, Mia, are constantly traveling and moving, as their mother is a professor (their father is as well, but the parents are divorced). The girls show up in London, and the first person their mother introduces them to? Surprise - her boyfriend! Whom she will be marrying, and Liv and Mia will being moving in to his house. Liv's soon-to-be stepbrother, is a strange, quite one, and her soon-to-be-stepsister is pushy and a bit rude, and her soon-to-be-stepfather is old and just a bother in general. Attending school means meeting new people, and Liv immediately meets Grayson's friends - Arthur, Jasper, and Henry. Things get weird when Liv starts dreaming, and the four boys are in her dreams. Or she's in theirs. When they want her to join their strange dream group, Liv is skeptical, but she joins. But perhaps things aren't so plausible - perhaps things are much more sinister than they appear...<br /><br />One thing that strikes me in all of Gier's books is the humor. I love how funny Liv's voice is, how Gier makes Liv a tiny bit awkward, a lot sweet, and a bit sarcastic, in a funny way. This book is hilarious, even if there are parts that are very serious, and borderline scary.<br /><br />I liked Liv. She has a distinct voice, and it's so great to watch the story unfold from her perspective. She likes logic and science, and likes to figure things out. She joins the boys and their bizarre rituals, but mostly she wants to help them, and wants to prove to herself that demons aren't real. See, the boys tried to summon a demon who will grant their hearts' desire. On Halloween. Wild.<br /><br />I like the boys. There are four of them, one of them being the stepbrother (Grayson), the other three being his friends. They're all described as super good-looking, like shampoo commercial guys. Each has their own personality. Jasper is very rambunctious, and doesn't really take things seriously. Grayson is a bit protective. Arthur... he's an odd one (and you'll see why, at the end of this book). Henry is the mysterious and brooding one, but he's also very sweet.<br /><br />Another thing that I really liked about this book is the sister-sister relationship! Usually, the younger sister is SO ANNOYING, and I dislike her a lot (like, genuinely dislike her, not dislike her as the kid sister). Mia is about five years younger, but she's mature for her age, yet fun like a child should be. I liked her a lot, which surprised me. <br /><br />The story is quite interesting and goes by very quickly. I was really strapped for time this week (soooo many exams and papers and research), but I finished this one faster than I expected. I love how Gier writes - her writing is beautiful, but also very easy to read and pay attention to. Seriously, anyone could read her books, translated or not, and know her writing style and voice.<br /><br />There IS romance in this book! Check out my Swoon Thursday post from yesterday (March 12th) if you want a little insight on the romance. The love interest is pretty swoony, and he's more than a love interest - he plays quite pivotal roles in the book. No love triangle, and while Liv becomes infatuated with the love interest pretty quickly, I wouldn't call it insta-love. More like insta-interest. There are no declarations of love or serious feelings, so no insta-love. The romance is really sweet, but also very subtle and a bit in the background compared to the story.<br /><br />The story was intriguing and almost scary at some points! Dreams are beautiful and scary places. I didn't see the climax coming - and it occurs pretty late, around 90% of the book. But I couldn't stop reading. This book wraps up pretty nicely, but in a way that you KNOW there will be more books (hence, the Silver Trilogy). No cliffhanger though, yay!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Nothing in particular - I might have wanted a little more from the romance, but I know how Gier writes in the romance into the story of her books, and it's always very slow and subtle. Which is cool, I'm fine with that.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Yes! Great paranormal/fantasy read, set in the contemporary world. This one was fun and easy and quick, and not to mention lush in details and gorgeous in writing. And the cover is pretty great! I liked the original USA cover, but this new cover is spectacular. In any case, I'd recommend any Gier book I've read (now four), this one included!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4 stars. I'll definitely be reading book two as soon as I can get my hands on it! Noooow, please! I wonder if there are editions in Spanish (bilingual for the win!)... I'll buy one of those, if I have to!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11258183996215480007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And all the cutziness and fluffiness of this cloudy book got me out of the slump. <br/><br/><b>I mean who can resist the charms of dream traveling???</b><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503651956ra/23682902.gif' width='450' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>“All that we see or seem is but a dream within a dream.”</i><br/><br/>♥This book was full of gossipy shenanigans! Liv's life couldn't be any more cliche. Divorced, career-obsessed parents, a loving nanny, future ex-step father and his family</span>
  <span id="freeText13450933463012359177" style="display:none">Oh boy! <i>It was so refreshing! Just what I needed.</i> I hadn't read anything in months because I was in the WORST reading slump of my life. And all the cutziness and fluffiness of this cloudy book got me out of the slump. <br><br><b>I mean who can resist the charms of dream traveling???</b><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503651956ra/23682902.gif" width="450" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“All that we see or seem is but a dream within a dream.”</i><br><br>♥This book was full of gossipy shenanigans! Liv's life couldn't be any more cliche. Divorced, career-obsessed parents, a loving nanny, future ex-step father and his family, new school, gossip blog, four boys,yes mind you! <b>FOUR BOYS!</b> yada yada yada! But the narration! THE NARRATION!!! Liv's relatonship with Lottie(the nanny) and Mia(her sister) was LOVE! <br><br>♥Liv and her sister's life has always been in travel. They never had a home. Her mother's job never allowed them to settle in one place. And this year her mother is going to teach in Oxford and hence they all reached London! And there began the drama!<br><br><u>
  <b>THE SPENCERS</b>
</u> <br>Spencers are Liv's new family; future step-father and future step-siblings. Ernest is Liv's mother's new boyfriend and Florence and Grayson are his twins. I absolutely loved Grayson and absolutely hated Florence! <br><br><u>
  <b>THE SCHOOL</b>
</u><br>Frognal Academy is our MC's new private school. I loved her new school and her new friends even Persephone grew on me after some time. And the blog was such a fun to read!! <br><br><u>
  <b>THE BOYS</b>
</u><br>Henry, Grayson, Jasper, Arthur! I LOVED their gang! Their friendship! Everything about them. Even Jasper aka Shaving Fun Ken and boy he was <i>something</i>!!<br><br><u>
  <b>The DREAM-TRAVELING</b>
</u><br>I will give it to Kerstin Gier the idea of dream-traveling is freaking awesome and refreshing! I mean we can spy people in their dreams and do the inconceivable and change our shape and form and can be an owl or a panda or whatever we like!!! And we can wander all night in the dream corridor!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503652905ra/23682999.gif" width="450" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>THE DEMON</b>
</u><br>The demon and Anabel's thing was cool but stupid! <br><br><u>
  <b>Henry!</b>
</u><br>*swoons* <br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499137731ra/23195542.gif" width="450" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I loved him the moment I laid my eyes on him! I KNEW IT!! I KNEW IT!! Henry and Liv were so so soooo adorable I can't even! Henry and Liv and the DREAM-CORRIDOR! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503652905ra/23683000.gif" width="450" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>You are my heart's desire, Liv Silver!</b>
</i> <br><br>ASGFHJSAHFHBRYBHBRCVUYRHBVREULKKYKU!!! <br><br>If you haven't pick it up yet, what are you waiting for???!!!! <br><br><b>4 STARS</b><br><br></span>

<div id="review_2435067528" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2435067528" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2435067528?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435067528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2478109381724765891">Not as amazing as Ruby Red trilogy, but still such a fun book! The general idea really reminded me of The Raven Boys honestly, though it reads very differently. Kind of like a Gossip GIrl with paranormal elements set in London. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_752482638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752482638" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752482638?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783841421050" href="/book/show/17613457-silber">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the author, YA, and anyone skeptical enough about the genre</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=part_of_a_series">part_of_a_series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752482638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4613754334446559636"><em>This book has been translated into English, as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dream a Little Dream</a></em>. <br/><br/>Given my earnest attempts to avoid getting into yet another German YA, I honestly couldn't say why "<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17566243.Silber_Das_erste_Buch_der_Tr_ume__Silber___1_' title='Silber Das erste Buch der Träume (Silber, #1) by Kerstin Gier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Silber: Das erste Buch der Träume</a>" ended up on my reading list. The unusual cover of the German edition could be one of the reasons, as I was hoping for some modern surrealist stuff. Then again given the number of YA books on GR, maybe it's just a question of statistics.<br/><br/>I haven't researched either the author or the book before st</span>
  <span id="freeText4613754334446559636" style="display:none"><em>This book has been translated into English, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream a Little Dream</a></em>. <br><br>Given my earnest attempts to avoid getting into yet another German YA, I honestly couldn't say why "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17566243.Silber_Das_erste_Buch_der_Tr_ume__Silber___1_" title="Silber Das erste Buch der Träume (Silber, #1) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das erste Buch der Träume</a>" ended up on my reading list. The unusual cover of the German edition could be one of the reasons, as I was hoping for some modern surrealist stuff. Then again given the number of YA books on GR, maybe it's just a question of statistics.<br><br>I haven't researched either the author or the book before starting, and the brief glance over its reviews left me vaguely annoyed. Turns out I had apparently managed to choose the cheesiest of chart toppers, that everyone raves about... to say nothing of the romantic pairing possibilities.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419277753i/13025739._SX540_.jpg" alt="love triangle" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story begins with Liv and her sister Mia, returning from their summer holiday in Switzerland, ready to begin a promising new life in a cozy little cottage in Oxford. <br><br>That's the plan at any rate. Not only does Liv's swiss cheese souvenir attract the interest of a drug dog at the airport, but her mother also announces a slight change of plans... of the <em>new boyfriend</em> variety. Since their Oxford dream house wasn't quite so dreamy, they'd be moving into a posh London neighborhood instead, and attend the fancy (fictional) "Frognal Academy". All thanks to Ernest (the boyfriend), whose own two children are also <em>coincidentally</em> attending said school.<br><br>So far so bad, but then Liv manages to top it all by meeting the school's 4 most popular guys for an impromptu seance session at the Highgate Cemetery... in a dream.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419277543i/13025719.jpg" alt="Highgate Cemetery" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is narrated from Liv's perspective, peppered with lots of humorous quips which often had me giggling like mad. As unoriginal as the plot may sound, I greatly enjoyed our heroine's dream wanderings as well as the concept behind how things in the dream world worked... or didn't work. Though I didn't find any memorable one-liners, the generally funny undertone of the story definitely helped boost its rating by at least a star.<br><br>The ending was very satisfying, though some reviewers criticize it due to distinct lack of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[demonic activity <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, it didn't bother me. The characters were quite interesting, and to a certain degree also likable; even the annoying ones (like Persephone and Florence).<br><br>My favorite character here was probably Mia, inspite of her small "screen time" she had the best lines:<br><blockquote>
<br>"We are also extremely excited to be here", said Mia, after a few seconds of embarrassed staring. "Is there at least something good to eat?"<br><br>"Does Mrs Finchley still collect those lovely porcelain figurines?"<br>I was contemplating whether I could answer with yet another "Yes, very interesting," without seeming obnoxious, but Mia had already answered: <br>"No! She's now collecting quite horrible and cheesy stuff. Some imbecilic-looking dancers."<br><br>"She's American. She could be a marriage dodger, or a psychopath,or …"<br>"… messy, kleptomaniac, republican, Jehova's Witness …" I suggested.<br>"That's not funny," said Florence.<br>"Do you have anything against Jehova's Witnesses?", asked Mia innocently.<br><br>"And now tell me, is your dad an internationally wanted terrorist or a serial killer?" Mia inquired sweetly behind me.<br>
</blockquote><br><br>The main reason for that 'lost' star, are minor issues, but they added up by the end of the book. For example - the narrator's rather odd fascination with eye colors:<br>- lots of "lit up" eyes <br>- Henry's slate gray eyes<br>- Grayson's caramel-candy-colored eyes<br>- and last but not least Anabel's amazing turquoise-colored eyes<br><br>On the whole lots of fun, perhaps a bit reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener">Gossip Girl</a> due to the mysterious Secrecy, who regularly airs Frognal Academy's dirty laundry on the <a href="http://www.tittletattleblog.de/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tittle-Tattle Blog</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419277543i/13025720.jpg" alt="XOXO Gossip Girl" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Verdict: 4/5 stars</strong><br>Suffice to say, I liked it enough to <em>immediately</em> pick up the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18161523.Silber_Das_zweite_Buch_der_Tr_ume__Silber___2_" title="Silber Das zweite Buch der Träume (Silber, #2) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das zweite Buch der Träume</a>.<br><br>============================================<br>review of the 2nd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1007207262" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das zweite Buch der Träume</a><br>review of the 3rd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1123920528" rel="nofollow noopener">Silber: Das dritte Buch der Träume</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1271362115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271362115" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1271362115?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37766180-mary?shelf=covers-i-fell-in-love-with">covers-i-fell-in-love-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37766180-mary?shelf=faves">faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1271362115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10425403943299548313">5/5 stars<br/><br/><b> The most interesting things are always the most dangerous </b><br/><br/><u> dream </u><br/><i>
  <b>noun</b>
</i><br/><i>1. a series of thoughts, images, and sensations occurring in a person's mind during sleep.<br/>2. a cherished aspiration, ambition, or ideal. </i><br/><br/>That was exactly what this beauty was. A dream.<br/>It had everything a perfect Halloween read has. Scary things, like whispers in the dark, shadows lurking in abandoned corridors, demonic rituals and stalkers. Fun, sass and an a totally amazing main character who made me crack up wit</span>
  <span id="freeText10425403943299548313" style="display:none">5/5 stars<br><br><b> The most interesting things are always the most dangerous </b><br><br><u> dream </u><br><i>
  <b>noun</b>
</i><br><i>1. a series of thoughts, images, and sensations occurring in a person's mind during sleep.<br>2. a cherished aspiration, ambition, or ideal. </i><br><br>That was exactly what this beauty was. A dream.<br>It had everything a perfect Halloween read has. Scary things, like whispers in the dark, shadows lurking in abandoned corridors, demonic rituals and stalkers. Fun, sass and an a totally amazing main character who made me crack up with laughter in her every quote. A unique love story, filled with magic, cuteness and passion, that made me smile and blush, and ship Liv and Henry. Villains unlike any others, secrets and twists, and a cover that made me take millions of pictures.<br><br>The writing was light, warm and gripping, the plot was unpredictable and left me with a million questions, the characters were all lovable and unique in their own way and the magic was careful, unique and well-written. I have to admit that at first, I had a fear that this book would remind me of Raven Boys, but in an inferior way, and I kept wondering if I'll like it but when I started reading, I realized it's actually pretty different from TRC but equally lovable. The small size of the book makes it a quick read for those who don't have enough time but want to read something spooky for the month.<br><br>I just can't explain with enough words what a wonderful experience it was. I always clicked with books about dreams, and Kerstin Gier's lovely sense of humor made it even more fabulous. I devoured this beauty in four days and was so happy about it that I kept mentioning it to every conversation I had. I also have a theory about who Secrecy might be, and I would love to share it with those who want to learn. I am not gonna add it in here because it's a long explanation.<br><br>In the second book, I would really love to see how the dream powers is explained, get a few glimpses of Liv's father perhaps, explore more of the dreamworld, live adventures, solve mysteries, enjoy sarcasm and jokes and fangirl about Liv and Henry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382653674ra/6097065.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I definitely recommend this if you want to read something quick but also very spooky and in-the-mood ♥<br><br>Be strong and wonderful and spooky, guys ♥ And never let anyone bring you down ♥<br>~Mary</span>
  <a data-text-id="10425403943299548313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1645014854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1645014854" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1645014854?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790277" href="/book/show/21469090-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=young-adult-genre">young-adult-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=angels-demons">angels-demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645014854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2812842210297237386"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_' title='Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dream a Little Dream</a> is the first installment in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/298438.Kerstin_Gier' title='Kerstin Gier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kerstin Gier</a>'s young adult, fantasy series titled <u>The Silver Trilogy</u>. The paranormal aspect allows the phrase, "I'll see you in my dreams" to take on an entirely different meaning in this book. It was pretty awesome. Ms. Gier's creativity was not news to me but I was still pleasantly surprised to read a plotline I have never, ever seen before in YA fiction. Thank you Ms. Gier! <br/><br/><b>My favorite quote:</b><br/><i>"Sometimes mom was faster than the iPad and she knew </i></span>
  <span id="freeText2812842210297237386" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_" title="Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream a Little Dream</a> is the first installment in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/298438.Kerstin_Gier" title="Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Kerstin Gier</a>'s young adult, fantasy series titled <u>The Silver Trilogy</u>. The paranormal aspect allows the phrase, "I'll see you in my dreams" to take on an entirely different meaning in this book. It was pretty awesome. Ms. Gier's creativity was not news to me but I was still pleasantly surprised to read a plotline I have never, ever seen before in YA fiction. Thank you Ms. Gier! <br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>"Sometimes mom was faster than the iPad and she knew at least as much as Wikipedia."</i><br><br><u>The Silver Trilogy</u> includes the following installments as of May 2016:<br>#1-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_" title="Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream a Little Dream</a><br>#2-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23179355.Dream_On__The_Silver_Trilogy___2_" title="Dream On (The Silver Trilogy, #2) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream On</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_" title="Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1421615136s/21469090.jpg" alt="Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23179355.Dream_On__The_Silver_Trilogy___2_" title="Dream On (The Silver Trilogy, #2) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <span id="freeText11448637396224792568" style="display:none">What kind of ending was that? good thing I own book two! <br /><br />It was a fun read and I really really enjoyed Liv'a character so much.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1302834499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11685912994828954262">This book was a lot darker than I expected. I originally read it because I needed a light book after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210722.The_Joys_of_Motherhood' title='The Joys of Motherhood by Buchi Emecheta' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Joys of Motherhood</a>, but quickly found out that the story between Kerstin Gier's latest trilogy is definitely <u>NOT</u> a feel good YA book. <br/><br/>The story itself revolves around a group of male friends who have unleashed a demon on Halloween with the usual bad results. Unfortunately, they lost their "virgin sacrifice" and need to replace her with a new member to re-up their blood circle and get</span>
  <span id="freeText11685912994828954262" style="display:none">This book was a lot darker than I expected. I originally read it because I needed a light book after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210722.The_Joys_of_Motherhood" title="The Joys of Motherhood by Buchi Emecheta" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Joys of Motherhood</a>, but quickly found out that the story between Kerstin Gier's latest trilogy is definitely <u>NOT</u> a feel good YA book. <br /><br />The story itself revolves around a group of male friends who have unleashed a demon on Halloween with the usual bad results. Unfortunately, they lost their "virgin sacrifice" and need to replace her with a new member to re-up their blood circle and get the demon back on this side of the void. That's where the main character, Liv, comes in. As usual, Kerstin Gier has written a feisty and comical lead for her story and Liv continuously goes toe-to-toe with her male co-characters in terms of witty comebacks and innovative plans. While the book does go a bit overboard with eligible love interest for me, I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /><br />For me, this book was a nice light read with the added benefit of plot twist that were scary as all heck. However, keep in mind I'm not a person who reads/watches/indulges in horror or ghost stories of any kind so if you do then this book will probably be the equivalent of you watching an episode of Barney. Nevertheless, the book was a good start to a trilogy. <br /><br />If you enjoyed this book, check out the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12411635.The_Nightmare_Affair__The_Arkwell_Academy___1_" title="The Nightmare Affair (The Arkwell Academy, #1) by Mindee Arnett" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Nightmare Affair</a> or Kerstin Gier's other Precious Stones series.<br /></span>
